**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy HTTP Filter Chain Registration and Execution

## Your Task

Trace how HTTP filter chains are registered and executed in the Envoy proxy. Find C++ and protobuf files across envoyproxy/envoy and envoyproxy/data-plane-api that implement: the FilterChainFactory interface (in envoy/http/), the FilterChainHelper that constructs chains from config, the FilterManager that executes filter chains at runtime, and the HttpConnectionManager proto that defines the filter_chain configuration schema.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

64-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced and documented the HTTP filter chain registration and execution flow in Envoy. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Components Identified:

### **Configuration (Data Plane API)**
- **HttpConnectionManager proto** (`http_connection_manager.proto` line 43, 471): Defines the filter chain configuration schema with `http_filters` field
- **HttpFilter proto** (lines 1339-1383): Defines individual filter configuration structure

### **Registration (C++ Implementation)**
- **FilterChainFactory interface** (`envoy/http/filter_factory.h`): Abstract interface for creating HTTP filter chains
- **FilterChainHelper template** (`filter_chain_helper.h`): Processes filter configurations during initialization
- **HttpConnectionManagerConfig** (`config.cc`): Creates filter configuration providers from proto

### **Execution (Runtime)**
- **FilterManager** (`filter_manager.h`): Manages both decoder and encoder filter chains for each HTTP stream
- **FilterChainUtility** (`filter_chain_helper.cc`): Instantiates actual filter chains when streams arrive
- **FilterChainManager interface**: Allows applying filter factory callbacks

## Execution Flow:

1. **Registration**: HttpConnectionManagerConfig parses `http_filters` from protobuf using FilterChainHelper, creating a list of filter configuration providers
2. **Creation**: When a new HTTP stream arrives, FilterManager is instantiated
3. **Chain Building**: FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories iterates through stored filter factories and applies them via FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb
4. **Execution**: Filters process data through decodeHeaders, decodeData, decodeTrailers methods with filters applied in configured order

Looks up the registered filter factory by type URL (line 134)\\n3. Creates a FilterConfigProvider that wraps the factory callback (line 155-156)\\n4. Stores these providers in a FilterFactoriesList for later execution\\n\\nThe FilterChainHelper uses the FilterConfigProviderManager to create static or dynamic filter configuration providers. For static filters, a factory callback (FilterFactoryCb, defined in envoy/http/filter_factory.h:24) is created immediately from the proto config.\\n\\n## Execution Flow at Runtime\\n\\n### Filter Chain Creation\\nWhen a new HTTP stream arrives at ConnectionManagerImpl (source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h), the newStream method is invoked. This creates an ActiveStream which instantiates a FilterManager (source/common/http/filter_manager.h:638-800). The FilterManager implements the FilterChainManager interface (envoy/http/filter_factory.h:70-81).\\n\\nThe HttpConnectionManager's FilterChainFactory implementation (which is the HttpConnectionManagerConfig) calls createFilterChain, which invokes FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.cc:17-47). This utility method:\\n1. Iterates through the stored FilterFactoriesList\\n2. For each filter factory provider, retrieves the actual FilterFactoryCb\\n3. Calls FilterManager::applyFilterFactoryCb (source/common/http/filter_manager.h:697) which applies each factory callback\\n4. Each callback creates filter instances and adds them to the decoder or encoder filter chains\\n\\n### Filter Execution\\nOnce the filter chain is constructed, filters are executed as data flows through the stream:\\n- `decodeHeaders` (line 748): Processes request headers through decoder filters\\n- `decodeData` (line 758): Processes request body through decoder filters  \\n- `decodeTrailers` (line 767): Processes request trailers through decoder filters\\n\\nThe FilterManager maintains separate lists of decoder_filters and encoder_filters (LinkedList structures). Decoder filters are applied in the order they are configured. Encoder filters are applied in reverse order (prepended rather than appended) so that the last configured filter is the outermost in the encoding chain.\\n\\n## Key Interfaces\\n\\n1. **FilterChainFactory** (envoy/http/filter_factory.h:89): Abstract interface with createFilterChain and createUpgradeFilterChain methods. Implemented by HttpConnectionManagerConfig to instantiate filter chains on demand.\\n\\n2. **FilterChainManager** (envoy/http/filter_factory.h:70): Interface for applying filter factory callbacks. Implemented by FilterManager to handle filter instantiation.\\n\\n3. **FilterManager** (source/common/http/filter_manager.h:638): Manages both decoder and encoder filter chains for a single HTTP stream, coordinating data flow through all configured filters.\\n\\n4. **FilterChainHelper** (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h:68): Template utility that processes filter configurations and creates filter configuration providers during setup.\\n\\n5. **FilterChainUtility** (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h:42): Static utility providing createFilterChainForFactories method that instantiates the actual filter chain at stream time.\\n\\nThis architecture allows Envoy to:\\n- Support dynamic filter configuration through config providers\\n- Enable per-filter error handling\\n- Maintain filter execution order consistently across requests\\n- Support both statically configured and dynamically discovered filters (ECDS)\"\n}\n",
